  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_aebc0e3a-658f-412a-a2db-eb6e0c93270c'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer6103120815138709431">There's a new vampire in town. His name is Valentine Maxwell. Goth-girl Raven knows this latest intruder can only mean trouble--he's the younger sibling of two vampires she fought to drive out of Dullsville. But when her brother, Billy, befriends this dangerous tween night prowler, the stakes are suddenly higher. Though torn by the excitement of every teen girl's fantasy--</span>
  <span id="freeText6103120815138709431" style="display:none">There's a new vampire in town. His name is Valentine Maxwell. Goth-girl Raven knows this latest intruder can only mean trouble--he's the younger sibling of two vampires she fought to drive out of Dullsville. But when her brother, Billy, befriends this dangerous tween night prowler, the stakes are suddenly higher. Though torn by the excitement of every teen girl's fantasy--attending the prom with her boyfriend--Raven must do everything she can to protect Billy.<br /><br />Valentine's appearance may pose even further threats. Could he somehow know Raven's innermost feelings about becoming immortal for her true love, Alexander? The far-from-ordinary romance of these two teen outsiders takes another surprise-filled spin in the fourth book of Ellen Schreiber's applauded Vampire Kisses series.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2837340520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer799481595262048883">This is one of my fave throwbacks to my teen years - Ellen Schreiber and her Vampire Kisses series. To say I was obsessed with this series is an absolute understatement. Recently, I picked this book up again and decided to throw myself into this series, and I still love it!<br/><br/>This series is full of cute-sy YA romance with Alexander and Raven. The book is written for a younger audience, but if you're like me and love sinking away into a fantastical world then it will be no issue to you. If you're ex</span>
  <span id="freeText799481595262048883" style="display:none">This is one of my fave throwbacks to my teen years - Ellen Schreiber and her Vampire Kisses series. To say I was obsessed with this series is an absolute understatement. Recently, I picked this book up again and decided to throw myself into this series, and I still love it!<br /><br />This series is full of cute-sy YA romance with Alexander and Raven. The book is written for a younger audience, but if you're like me and love sinking away into a fantastical world then it will be no issue to you. If you're expecting a "True Blood-esque" novel, then you've come to the wrong place.<br /><br />The fourth book in this series, Dance with a Vampire, continues Alexander and Raven's epic love story. Except, this time around we've got more crazy antics that the pair have to deal with. Valentine is now up to her trouble, making it seem impossible for our love birds to have a happy ending. <br /><br />A note for the reader: These books are relatively short, which makes them a fun, sweet, and smooth read. It's really easy to binge all of these books in a day if you have the nerve to. I read the first four books (back in the day) on a bus ride to a school swim meet. I re-read these books many times because of how short and fun they were. So, it's not a big time commitment if you read these babies one by one.<br /><br />Final note: The manga version of this series was one of the first mangas I ever read and made me fall in love with that "genre" (is genre the right word? Probably not). The pictures were beautiful, the story was magical and I'm glad it got me so into reading! Thank you Ellen for being one of my early reading addictions. Hopefully I'll find some more newer books by her soon! Her writing just vibes well with my reading style.<br /><br />I'd highly recommend these books. They are on the younger side of YA, but they are funny, sassy and absolutely adorable. My biggest con for this whole series was that it ended! I loved each book and I really want more by this author. So many YA novels take themselves way to seriously and try to make the teen be an adult. This series makes Raven be a fun, young girl who makes mistakes along the way (but she somehow gets an epic romance out of it).<br /><br />Five out of five stars!</span>
  <a data-text-id="799481595262048883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_248865163" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/248865163" />
    <a title="Emma (BelleBooks)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4783841-emma-bellebooks"><img alt="Emma (BelleBooks)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295267223p2/4783841.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/248865163?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma (BelleBooks)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma (BelleBooks)" href="/user/show/4783841-emma-bellebooks">Emma (BelleBooks)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer248865163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7594377256435038027">(Review for Books 1-8)<br/><br/>I decided to review all eight of these books together, as I pretty much read them all back to back and I don't think I would be able to go back and review them all individually.<br/><br/>Firstly, this is a series that I had known about for a while, but wasn't really too sure what the books were about. Going from the titles it's obvious that they are about vampires, but apart from that I hadn't really looked into them too much. One day in December, bored I decided to give the first bo</span>
  <span id="freeText7594377256435038027" style="display:none">(Review for Books 1-8)<br /><br />I decided to review all eight of these books together, as I pretty much read them all back to back and I don't think I would be able to go back and review them all individually.<br /><br />Firstly, this is a series that I had known about for a while, but wasn't really too sure what the books were about. Going from the titles it's obvious that they are about vampires, but apart from that I hadn't really looked into them too much. One day in December, bored I decided to give the first book a go and see how I liked it.<br /><br />All eight books are very short, not as short as a novella. But they are short, I'm pretty sure I averaged about 2 of these books a day while I was reading them. Although they are short they are enjoyable.<br />I would say they are aimed at a much younger audience than typical YA books. The writing in them is simple and straightforward making them that much easier to glide through one book to the next in the series, to me they all seemed to tie together which makes writing individual reviews on them too hard.<br /><br />The main character Raven is likeable and funny. Although she does come across very young and immature for her age. I am used to reading YA novels where the female main character is usually much wiser and mature for her age. This is another reason why I feel these books are marketed to the tween market.<br /><br />The plot itself is captivating and is full of twists and turns. There are quite a few laugh out loud moments as well which keeps the tone of the book rather light hearted. I did enjoy the different aspects of all the books, and the introducing of the new vampires to the town. I really liked the idea of the covenant ceremony to bond vampires for life, that was something I haven't really seen much of in other vampire books.<br /><br />There isn't really anything negative to say about these books at all, they are fun, light and easy to read. I'm glad I read them all back to back as I don't think I would go back to them if I had only read one or two, they don't really have that captivating element some YA series's do, although they are enjoyable.<br /><br />To me they were a nice break from some my heaver and thicker books that I need to get through, which was just what I needed at the time I read them. I am looking forward to the release of book 9 in the series, which I think is the last one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7594377256435038027" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_550230208" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/550230208" />
    <a title="Wren " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11442507-wren"><img alt="Wren " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443235719p2/11442507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/550230208?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wren " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wren " href="/user/show/11442507-wren">Wren </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=character-sweet-and-respectful-guys">character-sweet-and-respectful-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=halloween-book-challenge-2016">halloween-book-challenge-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer550230208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9173296115845013052">This review can also be found at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://fortheloveofbooksreviews.blogspot.ca/2016/11/dance-with-vampire-by-ellen-schreiber.html'>http://fortheloveofbooksreviews.blogs...</a><br/><br/><br/><br/> In this continuation of Raven and Alexander's story, Valentine Maxwell, Jagger's younger brother, has arrived in Dullsville and appears to be targeting Raven's brother. Raven fears that this might be some sort of revenge plot because of the issues that she, Alexander, and Valentine's siblings dealt with in the past, so with Alexander's help, she tries to uncover what's going on. <br/><br/>At the same time, Raven is having doubts and</span>
  <span id="freeText9173296115845013052" style="display:none">This review can also be found at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://fortheloveofbooksreviews.blogspot.ca/2016/11/dance-with-vampire-by-ellen-schreiber.html">http://fortheloveofbooksreviews.blogs...</a><br /><br /><br /><br /> In this continuation of Raven and Alexander's story, Valentine Maxwell, Jagger's younger brother, has arrived in Dullsville and appears to be targeting Raven's brother. Raven fears that this might be some sort of revenge plot because of the issues that she, Alexander, and Valentine's siblings dealt with in the past, so with Alexander's help, she tries to uncover what's going on. <br /><br />At the same time, Raven is having doubts and worries about her dream of becoming a vampire. She wants to be with Alexander and she knows that he loves her just as much as she loves him, so when Valentine threatens to tell her vampire lover about her secret worries, she fears that her relationship with him might become more complicated, or that it might not even survive at all. <br /><br />The Vampire Kisses series is such an enjoyable series. The books are perfect for when you want a short read after tackling a long, complex book or if you're trying to ease yourself from a reading slump. While the writing style might be a bit simpler than in other young adult books, it's still a great read for fans of vampire love stories. <br /><br />Even at the fourth volume in this series, Raven is still the funny, quirky, unique character that was introduced to readers in the first book. She is so, so likeable, and I find her sense of style, her hopes and dreams, and her love for vampires endearing. She actually reminds me a lot of myself. It's nice to have goths or alternative individuals within fiction that aren't the personification of the gloom-and-doom stereotype. <br /><br />Alexander remains the somewhat cliche, swoon-worthy, gothic vampire, love interest that Raven fell for in the first book. I find him just as endearing as Raven, with his romantic gestures and dark style. However, I have to say that I was a bit disappointed with his character in this novel. I was considering Raven's fear that Alexander would, for whatever reason, reject her when she admitted her worries about becoming a vampire. This made me wonder what might be going on in their relationship, if he might not be as sweet as the author shows us on the page. I mean, I think most people would make sure that their partners don't think they might leave them over legitimate fears concerning becoming what is basically a whole other, paranormal or supernatural, species? It seems like common sense, and Alexander must have failed Raven in some way if she was worrying over this so much. <br /><br />This book ended with a rather sad cliffhanger, though not a hopeless one. I'm glad that I own the next book so that I can read about what happens next sooner rather than later! This is a series that I like to come back to, it's one that I think I'll read until it ends. <br /><br />Overall, a very enjoyable book. While it raises somewhat frustrating questions concerning Raven and Alexander's relationship, I honestly think that these questions add some intrigue and a bit of suspense to the story. <br /><br />I recommend this series to fans of YA vampire romances. If you're looking for a short paranormal read, this series is for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9173296115845013052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_232376030" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/6897347-jen">Jen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6897347-jen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6897347-jen?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6897347-jen?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer232376030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14311813508418806390"><b>Favourite Character:</b> Alexander<br/><br/>This book was okay, it wasn't anything to write home about. Nothing big really happened. And the on-going feud between Trevor and Raven is getting old, I mean she loves Alexander and it's clear Trevor has had a big ol' crush on her for a while... Other than that Raven is starting to annoy me, at first her antics and immaturity were refreshing, but now it's like okay... 16 year olds do NOT act like this. I mean most of them are out having sex and doing drugs and rais</span>
  <span id="freeText14311813508418806390" style="display:none"><b>Favourite Character:</b> Alexander<br /><br />This book was okay, it wasn't anything to write home about. Nothing big really happened. And the on-going feud between Trevor and Raven is getting old, I mean she loves Alexander and it's clear Trevor has had a big ol' crush on her for a while... Other than that Raven is starting to annoy me, at first her antics and immaturity were refreshing, but now it's like okay... 16 year olds do NOT act like this. I mean most of them are out having sex and doing drugs and raising all kinds of hell, not pining over the fact that they don't know whether they want to be a vampire or not... Then again, 16 year olds in the real world don't have the option to be a vampire... At any rate, I mean she's 16 and Becky and Raven have hinted at sex twice in 4 books, it's like they aren't even thinking about it, which it crazy because what teenager isn't thinking about it, especially if they have a serious on-going relationship with someone.<br /><br />Another complaint I have is wtf is up with Alexander's eyes? In the first book they were midnight blue, now when it came to the third book it was said that they were chocolate a couple of times and charcoal once and now in the fourth book they are either blue or brown? I mean does the author not remember what colour they are? Do they change colour? And if they do change colour why weren't readers told about it?<br /><br />Also, wth is up with the days of the week, there was one part in the book where Raven and Alexander were going out and Henry and Billy were at home doing homework. It was a Friday night, yet the NEXT day Raven had school with Becky... I mean, if it wasn't the next day, there was no indication that the weekend had even passed... It was pretty much they went out to the cave, crap happened, they came home and Raven didn't sleep well and the next day she was tired at school. I mean I don't know much about the school system in what I assume is the U.S. but I'm pretty sure kids don't go to school on Saturdays.<br /><br />Other then these annoyances I found myself only reading the book because I needed to go to sleep at night and had nothing else better to do. If the fifth book isn't any better, I'm going to be disappointed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14311813508418806390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5320721172643128307">If you haven’t seen my other reviews for the books in this series I am just going to say it again, I love this series!<br/><br/>It isn’t always paradise dating a vampire and this is where problems start to arise for this cute goth couple.   <span id="freeText5320721172643128307" style="display:none">If you haven’t seen my other reviews for the books in this series I am just going to say it again, I love this series!<br /><br />It isn’t always paradise dating a vampire and this is where problems start to arise for this cute goth couple. I don’t even know what number I am on for rereading but it still hurts to see the problems that are tearing them apart. *sigh*<br /><br />We do get to see Raven be more of a sister towards her brother which is a nice mix into the vampire madness. We can’t really blame her from wanting to protect him from the undead though! I know I’d do the same, ha.<br /><br />Trevor, the typical jock, is still around and even though he doesn’t have much to do with this plot he is still trying to ruin Raven one dance at a time. I do have a soft spot for him because I just love the banter between them. Alexander will still always be my number and who I root for though.<br /><br />Overall, it was as good as the first time and I’m still excited to continue my reread through the series.</span>

<div id="review_508057841" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/508057841" />
    <a title="Alyson {Error Nebula}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8365976-alyson-error-nebula"><img alt="Alyson {Error Nebula}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388607087p2/8365976.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyson {Error Nebula}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyson {Error Nebula}" href="/user/show/8365976-alyson-error-nebula">Alyson {Error Nebula}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061778988" href="/book/show/5489683-dance-with-a-vampire">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Alyson by: </span>
      K. D. B.
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8365976-alyson-error-nebula?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8365976-alyson-error-nebula?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer508057841" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10537856431495012373">I don't want to start any arguments, as everyone have their own opinion, I just wanted to say this was the best book in the series so far. If you don't include bitchy valentine, that is.<br/><br/>To be fair, I suggest to read the first three books before reading this review for spoiler-free experience.<br/><br/>Jagger and Luna left Dullsville and all is good, until their little brother, Valentine Maxwell, shows up with an unknown goal. While Raven and Alexander have ups and downs because of the little Nosferatu, th</span>
  <span id="freeText10537856431495012373" style="display:none">I don't want to start any arguments, as everyone have their own opinion, I just wanted to say this was the best book in the series so far. If you don't include bitchy valentine, that is.<br><br>To be fair, I suggest to read the first three books before reading this review for spoiler-free experience.<br><br>Jagger and Luna left Dullsville and all is good, until their little brother, Valentine Maxwell, shows up with an unknown goal. While Raven and Alexander have ups and downs because of the little Nosferatu, the prom is coming up. And that's the reason why this book is called 'Dance with a Vampire'. You're welcome.<br><br><b>Plot:</b><br>The plot of this novel was more polished and entertaining than the last three books. Even though I feel the next books will be more action filled, I enjoyed even the little chapters with no actual meaning (yes, I liked the manicure chapter too. Revenge is best served... with black nailpolish!)<br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-KRIScwrIV90/UcFvadZiN5I/AAAAAAAAAcs/8LyQ93_rBRU/s1600/tumblr_inline_mjk9qj22UH1qz4rgp.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="179" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380405396ra/789648.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Writing:</b><br>The writing was light and humorous like in the previous books, but some dialogues you don't realize sometimes who is talking until you complete the entire conversation.<br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-0iv8eAH_3f8/UcFwKMTU87I/AAAAAAAAAc4/p9KQM5T9KMQ/s1600/tumblrm1rwfdpy231qfypok.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="181" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380405396ra/789649.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Romance:</b><br>Alright, finally, Raven and Alexander have actual problems in their goddamn relationship. They are finally showing signs of not-so-eternal love- Raven has a conflict of joining the dark underworld, while Alexander is craving for her blood and flesh.<br>Finally! I though it would be lovey-dovey one hundred percent until the end!<br><br><b>Black Lipstick- Raven:</b><br>Raven was just a plot device and a comic relief in this novel. Pretty pathetic if you ask me. She also whines about another girl buying the dress she wanted to prom and everyone are like 'we'll do anything for our little Raven'. I'm happy that the rest of the plot made me forget it.<br>And seriously, who sleeps with hungry vampires in a coffin?!<br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-QY_72J7DgPY/UcQ_H9ydJ3I/AAAAAAAAAdY/iDqDlG8P9Po/s1600/tumblr_inline_mjk9op46RT1qz4rgp.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380405396ra/789650.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Not so Gentleman- Alexander:</b><br>Alexander was, once again as in the first book, swoon worthy. He actually was craving for blood all along! Now you're a true vampire, Alexander!<br>But I do have to note that he still all hurt and shit because of the little stuff.<br><br><b>The Missing and Missed- Jagger and Luna:</b><br>I miss those two funky vampires! I really do hope they will come later in the series, or else.<br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-zupkWNKxJrM/UcRD_oWo5XI/AAAAAAAAAd0/lIvfZ-Kd2sw/s1600/tumblr_inline_mn21lcqVNv1qz4rgp.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="166" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380405396ra/789651.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>The not Amazing One- Valentine:</b><br>Valentine wasn't a strong point in this book. Let just say he was swallow, even for a vampire. But I do love his cool-- oops, I almost said a spoiler! Almost killed by fans...<br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-Jb8cyDxk47U/UcRE650cGyI/AAAAAAAAAeA/HMwecDV8qfM/s1600/tumblr_lvzfbgRfxv1r6twbno1_250.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380405396ra/789652.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Overall:</b><br>The plot was honestly way better than previous books. I hope to read Coffin Club next month, even though it's right on the shelf.<br><br><b>4.5 STARS<br><br>Liked:</b><br>-Alexander<br>-Plot<br>-Prom<br><br><b>Disliked:</b><br>-Where are the Maxwell's?!<br>-Raven<br>-Valentine <br><br><a href="http://bookreview4uguyz.blogspot.co.il/2013/06/review-dance-with-vampire-vampire.html" rel="nofollow noopener"> Review on my blog!:) </a></span>

<div id="review_112506243" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112506243" />
    <a title="Ash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2679967-ash"><img alt="Ash" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112506243?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash" href="/user/show/2679967-ash">Ash</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112506243" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer620057084357804504">I ask myself, what audience is this book being aimed at. I'm still test reading the series for the librarians at school who were keen to hear what they were like, and I feel so horrible having to say that I don't really like them at all. They're OK, that's the truth, but they are not brilliant. The premise of each book is simple - Human girl who wants to be a vampire meets a vampire boy and they fall in love. They are hunted by evil vampires who wish to make the girl one of them despite her love</span>
  <span id="freeText620057084357804504" style="display:none">I ask myself, what audience is this book being aimed at. I'm still test reading the series for the librarians at school who were keen to hear what they were like, and I feel so horrible having to say that I don't really like them at all. They're OK, that's the truth, but they are not brilliant. The premise of each book is simple - Human girl who wants to be a vampire meets a vampire boy and they fall in love. They are hunted by evil vampires who wish to make the girl one of them despite her loves wishes and chaos ensues. That's there is the plot essentially of nearly all of the books, each with a slightly different setting and the introduction and subtraction of characters. Not too much changes plot wise and after four books which is kind of sad really, I just wish she got changed in the second book and the story could have actually gone somewhere. However I find myself simply confused, is this book aimed at a young adult audience, or a younger "tween" audience. I just can't tell, and I hope for the sake of this book that it's a "tween" audience, it just doesn't work at YA literature for me. <br /><br />The only remotely good thing about this series besides rather attractive male vampires is the relationship between Raven and her family. They love and accept her for who she is, even if Billy does make fun of her sometimes, it's in a fun cute way. Her relationship with Billy is one of the few things that changes in this book, it becomes stronger and her need to protect him from the vampire child he has become friends with increases, and in some ways her finally caring about someone other than herself or her "perfect" boyfriend is a good thing. I'm starting to think this is definitely a book for a younger audience... Just not sure yet. I'll let you know.<br /><br />1 Star.</span>
  <a data-text-id="620057084357804504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8256653020615122444">Another book done in this painful series. Every book so far we've had a different vampire and the same plot. <br/><br/>This time, we have Valentine who is Jagger and Luna's little brother.   <span id="freeText8256653020615122444" style="display:none">Another book done in this painful series. Every book so far we've had a different vampire and the same plot. <br /><br />This time, we have Valentine who is Jagger and Luna's little brother. He tried to get close to Billy and we all know what happens there. <br /><br />I cannot stand some of these characters. Becky really bothered me in this book. Her and Matt have been together basically since the end of the first book, and I feel like we have seen her become more and more reliant. She seems to always be in a panic to see him in the mornings and every freaking second of the day. The whole bit with not wanting to keep a secret was ridiculous. You're like 17, it's normal to have secrets or not give yourself completely to some boy you've been dating for a few months. Characters like her encourage young women to be reliant and men, I'm not for it. <br /><br />I think Raven really let's us down in this book. Thank God she's not as annoying as she has been in the other books but I feel like she's being a little bit of a hypocrite with the whole vampire situation. I just want her to shut up and become one already. <br /><br />Cringing through it, but I'm going to keep going <br /><br /></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer328302716" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer544910469900760537">Dance with a Vampire was a fantastic installment to the Vampire Kisses series. Alexander and Raven might have gotten rid of Luna and Jagger, but a new vampire is in town, Valentine. As far as villain characters go, Valentine is pretty tame. He reads thoughts and spreads secrets to stir up trouble in Raven and Alexander's relationship. My favorite character is Raven. I like her style and attitude. She dresses and acts how she wants to and doesn't care what anyone else thinks. Alexander has become</span>
  <span id="freeText544910469900760537" style="display:none">Dance with a Vampire was a fantastic installment to the Vampire Kisses series. Alexander and Raven might have gotten rid of Luna and Jagger, but a new vampire is in town, Valentine. As far as villain characters go, Valentine is pretty tame. He reads thoughts and spreads secrets to stir up trouble in Raven and Alexander's relationship. My favorite character is Raven. I like her style and attitude. She dresses and acts how she wants to and doesn't care what anyone else thinks. Alexander has become my new book boyfriend. His goth style, being a vampire, and caring attitude make him very swoon worthy. The plot flows elegantly, thanks to the author's talented writing style. I couldn't put the book down. The ending made me a little agitated. I can't wait to pick up the next book in the series and find out what happens next. </span>
  <a data-text-id="544910469900760537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2326738700" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3439580142634134523">This is the 4th book in the Vampire Kisses series and it continues the adventure with Raven, her vampire boyfriend Alexander and friends. In this book, there is another pale stranger running around town and he is much younger and has now befriended Raven's little brother. Lots of mystery, twists and turns, and even a Prom. I don't want to go into the story more as not to spoil it but I do recommend this book and series to all vampire lovers.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55485617-kristyn?shelf=book-series">book-series</a>,

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2992320645002421168">This book in the series focused more on the sibling relationship of Raven and Billy. I love that because I, too, have a little brother. Raven is very much Mother Hen (kind of like me) where she likes to pick on her little brother, but at the same time want to protect him. I liked reading about love that wasn't centered on romantic.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1959506290" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1959506290" />
    <a title="Rants and Bants" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24862580-rants-and-bants"><img alt="Rants and Bants" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541473603p2/24862580.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1959506290?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rants and Bants" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rants and Bants" href="/user/show/24862580-rants-and-bants">Rants and Bants</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=boys-boys-boys">boys-boys-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=childhood-books">childhood-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=the-plot-hooked-me">the-plot-hooked-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=girls-girls-girls">girls-girls-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=halloween-reading">halloween-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=european">european</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1959506290&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1959506290" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16502933345305245344"><br/><br/>Valentine is the newest character introduced in here. I actually like him more than Jagger and Luna. I think he’s adorable, even though he’s nefarious, because he’s a little monster who just wants to find his older siblings again and thinks Raven and Alexander are responsible. There were more references in here, some made up and some I recognized: “Morbid Monkey” (made up), Mindfreak, “studded black cargo pants with chains” (I think she means Tripp pants), Ville Valo (lead singer of HIM), etc. B</span>
  <span id="freeText16502933345305245344" style="display:none"><br /><br />Valentine is the newest character introduced in here. I actually like him more than Jagger and Luna. I think he’s adorable, even though he’s nefarious, because he’s a little monster who just wants to find his older siblings again and thinks Raven and Alexander are responsible. There were more references in here, some made up and some I recognized: “Morbid Monkey” (made up), Mindfreak, “studded black cargo pants with chains” (I think she means Tripp pants), Ville Valo (lead singer of HIM), etc. Basically my life as a high school student. Oh Raven—we would’ve been best friends. I’d had another friend named Raven and also friends with those interests, but unfortunately they were kind of abusive, not friendly like you.<br /><br />Raven draws? I didn’t know this, but one more reason to like her. <br /><br />Becky’s place is actually much nicer than I’d thought it would be. I thought it was implied she was poor, but I guess she’s just rural, which isn’t the same thing. It’s nice that there is more girl time between them. Not going to lie though, I do get annoyed with Becky with basically not wanting to keep a secret for Raven just for herself, and having to include Matt in everything. Can’t some things just stay between the two of them? Especially since Becky just met Matt and she’s known Raven her whole life?<br /><br />I could’ve sworn Raven’s first encounter with Valentine was actually him appearing in her house in the hallway without anyone else knowing about it, but I guess I was wrong. There I go again with my weird non-memories.<br /><br /><u>Quotes of humor:</u><br />-“‘Yes, I would be frightened too. You’re only in fifth grade.’” After Raven picks up an Algebra textbook in her brother's room. Speaking of Billy, this is the first book that heavily involves him in the plot.<br />-“The creepy man’s eyes twinkled.” =) Jameson is so cute. This was when he got another date with Ruby. =)<br /><br />Prom actually seemed exciting in here, which is unusual (even made a Carrie reference!). Alexander, like Carrie, was nervous to go in. Not going to lie, sometimes I’m sort of critical at first with how careless they are, going to places even though there’s the chance that Alexander could be found out (with reflections, garlic, pictures, etc.), but it’s not like he was going to go apeshit on anyone like the Twihard vampires.<br /><br />Did I mention that Raven has the perfect parents? They’re kind, accepting of Alexander, supportive of her lifestyle (her mom encourages her to be social but also starts to realize that Raven has her own personality and style, and doesn’t want to be like others). I was glad the person at the pedicure/salon place started being accepting toward Raven too. It’s horrifying to me that they didn’t have black nail polish there ): <br /><br />Alexander wanted to see her world of being a student at school—and to be honest, it’s a different world to me too, considering it seems like the typical TV-type school and suburbian lifestyle that I never knew, growing up in a not-so-good area where things weren’t the nice normal kind of way that they are on TV and the stupid misbehaving kids (some of whom were scary) got to run everything because parents/teachers/admins didn’t do their jobs. But I digress. Basically, even though I also went to a public school like Raven, Alexander and I can both relate to how different her normal world is from ours. From her nice nuclear American family, to her basic cardboard cutout school lol.<br /><br />I still love this series (always will) but one of the things that annoyed me towards the end of this book was that Raven was making a big deal out of not being able to see Alexander for just a few days. Literally a few days. She was really sad and acting like it would be for a few years. It’s like…you’re going to have to be away from your boyfriend SOMETIMES. I don’t know, I think they’re too attached and it’s not the healthiest to be that attached. I just couldn’t get with the dramatics of that. But otherwise, another great book from another great series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16502933345305245344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2567633761" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2567633761" />
    <a title="Jacqueline Barber" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26615231-jacqueline-barber"><img alt="Jacqueline Barber" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588182932p2/26615231.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2567633761?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacqueline Barber" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacqueline Barber" href="/user/show/26615231-jacqueline-barber">Jacqueline Barber</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26615231-jacqueline-barber?shelf=owned-read">owned-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26615231-jacqueline-barber?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26615231-jacqueline-barber?shelf=complete-owned-series">complete-owned-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26615231-jacqueline-barber?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26615231-jacqueline-barber?shelf=four-stars">four-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2567633761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16116922931017043505">Just when you though it was safe to go back in the cemetery... BAM preteen Vampire! Raven and Alexander thought they had finally rid themselves and Dullsville of the Maxwell children when Billy Boy, Raven's tween brother, makes friends with the ghostly looking new kid in town. Alexander and Raven quickly realize that the miniature Jagger walking around is in fact Valentine, Jagger and Luna's little brother, and he has set his sights on Raven's brother. Our Gothic Heroine has a lot on her plate f</span>
  <span id="freeText16116922931017043505" style="display:none">Just when you though it was safe to go back in the cemetery... BAM preteen Vampire! Raven and Alexander thought they had finally rid themselves and Dullsville of the Maxwell children when Billy Boy, Raven's tween brother, makes friends with the ghostly looking new kid in town. Alexander and Raven quickly realize that the miniature Jagger walking around is in fact Valentine, Jagger and Luna's little brother, and he has set his sights on Raven's brother. Our Gothic Heroine has a lot on her plate from trying to spend time with her Vampire Prince, keeping her brother from being a late night snack, and prom she is a pretty busy girl. <br /><br />Maybe its his age (11), but there is a certain innocence that Valentine has that both Jagger and Luna lacked. There is just something about him that makes you want to take care of him. I mean hes only a kid and its kind of obvious that his motives for being in Dullsville is very different from his older siblings motives. He is just trying to find his siblings and reunite his family, something he blames Raven and Alexander for. Valentine had the ability to read people and know their own innermost thought something he uses to try and figure out where Jagger and Luna are. In order to get close to Raven he makes friends with Billy Boy and his Nerd Mate Henry. I love the Billy plays a bigger role in this book. Its obvious that he looks up to Raven and wants to be close to her even though they have drastically different personalities. Seeing the brother sister bond was super nice! Another thing that I love seeing is the relationship between Raven and Trevor. As much as I LOVE Raven and Alexander, I'm not going to lie I ma low key rooting for Raven and Trevor! They have a nice Yin and Yang thing going on and I'm here for it.   <br /><br />So far I think the 4th book is my favorite. You get to see Raven interact more with the "supporting" characters which is really nice and you also get to see more of Raven's internal conflict when it comes to actually becoming a vampire. This book is a good mid point to the series and I look forward to what happens next.      </span>
  <a data-text-id="16116922931017043505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HoVupkuHgoJ643AkH4x+06yuvcyejuSJK64lc2K1Hrrln+ImIMBW9HoIeia5zV7uV5zIZNjSjNkQ9VWn+iETpg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('s+PdA/R6Rmt5urM9luCFoMyevtNLPsN7UP9zZg54ndpI+VGDnz2SHXlRuT8woaWdN6zLew1iqytrpAOyluyQxg==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/153734.Ellen_Schreiber">About Ellen Schreiber</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/153734.Ellen_Schreiber"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_111x148-8060b12280b2aec7543bafb574ee8422.png);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/153734.Ellen_Schreiber">Ellen Schreiber
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
4,060
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9921533227443769102">Before I took pen to paper, I was an actress. I attended a local university majoring in theatre and spent a summer in London at the Royal Academy of Dramatic Arts where I learned about the “Old Bard” from amazingly talented teachers. <br/><br/>When I returned from London, I relocated to Chicago where I lived for five years. There, I graduated from the Second City Training Center and performed improv, Shakes</span>
  <span id="freeText9921533227443769102" style="display:none">Before I took pen to paper, I was an actress. I attended a local university majoring in theatre and spent a summer in London at the Royal Academy of Dramatic Arts where I learned about the “Old Bard” from amazingly talented teachers. <br /><br />When I returned from London, I relocated to Chicago where I lived for five years. There, I graduated from the Second City Training Center and performed improv, Shakespeare, comedies and dramas--I even sang and danced on a cruise boat--without falling in Lake Michigan! A classmate of mine from Second City and I created and performed a two woman show for a year before I braved it alone doing stand-up comedy. It was during this time I began to write an adult novel about a rock star--I had always enjoyed writing...<br /> <br />Fast forward a couple of years along with a move home where I was performing “stand-up” at comedy clubs in the area. On a plane to LA to decide my fate-- “to move to LA or not to move to LA” that is the question, my big bro, Mark, coincidentally with the same last name as mine (author of PRINCES IN EXILE, DREAMS OF THE SOLO TRAPEZE and STARCROSSED) handed me a young adult book he found at the library he thought I’d like to read during the flight.<br /> <br />As I read the book, I thought, ‘I can do this!’<br /> <br />I returned from LA, and instead of moving there, I wrote my story about the rock star as a young adult novel and called it JOHNNY LIGHTNING.<br />Mark, my writing mentor, edited JL for me. He was kind enough to send the manuscript to his publisher in Belgium--Facet--and they published it! In Dutch!<br /> <br /> I was now on a new life path!<br /> <br />In 2001 HarperCollins made me an offer I couldn’t refuse! Not only was HarperCollins going to publish TEENAGE MERMAID, but it was in a language I could read and book stores I could walk into! HarperCollins also bought VAMPIRE KISSES and COMEDY GIRL.<br /><br />It was a dream come true!<br /><br />Since beginning my new life path, VAMPIRE KISSES, TEENAGE MERMAID, and MY MOTHER, THE CLOWN have been published by Facet in Belgium and JOHNNY LIGHTNING has been published in Germany by Ravensburger. <br /> <br /> Then my fabulous editor at HarperCollins asked me for a sequel to VAMPIRE KISSES! <br />HarperCollins published VAMPIRE KISSES 2--KISSING COFFINS and now the soon to be released VAMPIRE KISSES 3--VAMPIREVILLE. I am currently writing VAMPIRE KISSES 4!<br /><br />When I'm not writing about the love affair between vampire obsessed, goth girl Raven and my favorite mysterious dark-eyed hottie, Alexander Sterling, I enjoy working on my other novels, shopping for Hello Kitty items, and attempting to gain control of the remote from my boyfriend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9921533227443769102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
